STATE'S ATTORNEY'S OFFICE RESPONSE REGARDING

Honorable Gregg Goslin

Cook County Board of Commissioners
11 8 North Clark Street, Room 567

3

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDfNGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

Re: President and Commissioner Vacancy Procedures
Dear Commissioner Goslin:
You have asked our office to advise you concerning the procedures authorized by law for appointing a
successor or replacement should a vacancy occur in the office of the President of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners, or in the office of one of the Cook County Commissioners. Specifically, you ask four
questions:
I address your questions in the order you pose them.
1. Should a vacancy occur in the Office of the President of the Cook County Board of
Commissioners, is the County Board authorized by law to appoint a replacement?

Section 4-8 of the Cook County Ordinance, and Section 5/2-6003 of the Counties Code, both titled,
"Vacancy in office of president," provide in pertinent part as follows:
In the case of death, resignation, removal from office or other inability to act of the
president so elected ... If less than two years and sixty days of the unexpired term remain,
the board of commissioners shall elect one of their number to serve the unexpired term of
the president.
55 ILCS 5/2-6003; Cook County Ord.ยง 4-8.
Based on these authorities, the County Board is authorized to appoint a replacement to fill a vacancy in
the office of President of the Cook County Board, when less than two years and sixty days of the
unexpired term remain.

2. If the Board of Commissioners has such appointive authority, must the appointee be a current
sitting commissioner, and if so, must said Commissioner be of the same political party as the
current President?
Based on the above cited authority, the Board's appointee as President of the Board must be a sitting
commissioner, but need not be of the same political party as the President whose tenn he or she is
appointed to complete.

3. Does the law provide for a timetable for an appointment, and require anything other than a
simple majority vote on the question?
Neither of the above cited authorities provide a timetable for appointment of a President by the Board
when less than two years and sixty days remain in the unexpired tenn of the President. Since no higher
majority is required by law, the appointment may be made by a simple majority vote. See, Board Rules,
secs. 1-5, 4-5.

4. Similarly, should a vacancy occur in the office of a Cook County Commissioner, who is
authorized by law to appoint a replacement?
Section 25- 11 of the Election Code, pertaining to vacancies in elective county office, expressly pennits
home rule counties such as Cook County to provide for fi lling vacancies by ordinance, for the office of
county commissioner. See, I 0 ILCS 5/25-1 1. The County Board has exercised this authority, adopting

4

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

Ordinance No. 94-0-18, titled "Ordinance to Establish Qualifications for Office and Filling of Vacancies
in Single-Member Districts," on March 1, 1994. That ordinance provides in pertinent part as follows:
Section 2. Vacancies

***

(b) At all times from and after December 5, 1994, if a vacancy occurs in the Office of
Commissioner, such vacancy shall be filled by appointment of the appropriate district
committee of the political party in the County Board District of which the incumbent was
a candidate at the time of his or her election. If the incumbent Commissioner was
appointed to the position, then such vacancy shall be filled by the appropriate district
committee of the political party in the County Board District which appointed the
incumbent. The appointee shall be of the same political party that the incumbent
Commissioner was at the time of his or her election or appointment.

(c) The district committee of a County Board District shall consist of the committeemen
of each ward or township contained in whole or in part within the County Board District.
In making appointments under this Section, each committeeman of the appropriate
district committee shall be entitled to one vote for each vote that was received, in that
portion of the County Board District which he or she represents on the committee, by the
Commissioner whose seat is vacant at the general election at which the Commissioner
was elected to the seat that has been vacated (or his or her elected predecessor, if the
Commissioner whose seat was vacant was appointed) and a majority of the total number
of votes received in such general election by the Commissioner whose seat is vacant is
required for the appointment of his or her successor.
(d) Appoinhnents made under this Section shall be in writing and shall be signed by
members of the district committee whose total votes are sufficient to make the
appointments. Such appointments shall be filed with the County Clerk.
Cook County Ord. No. 94-0-18, sec. 2{b), (c) & (d).
Thus, pursuant to the above cited ordinance, " the appropriate district committee of the political party in
the County Board District of which the incumbent was a candidate at the time of his election," is the
entity authorized to appoint a replacement for vacancy in the office of Commissioner.
If you have any further questions regarding this matter, please do not hesitate to contact me.
Yours truly,
Patrick T. Driscoll, Jr.
Deputy State's Attorney
Chief, Civil Actions Bureau

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the communication be received
and filed. The motion carried unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
EARLEAN COLLINS, County Commissioner

LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
COOK COUNTY JUVENILE TEMPORARY DETENTION CENTER STATUS
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII Section 6(a)
of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power and perfonn any function
pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, Cook County government has the responsibility for funding, operating and monitoring the
Cook County Juvenile Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to insuring the safety and welfare
of minors in accordance with Federal, State and local ordinances on juvenile detention; and
WHEREAS, over the past several years there has been increasing allegations in reference to the
treatment of children, the quality of staff, management and operating procedures which has resulted in
litigation; and
WHEREAS, the parties to litigation have been m talks to resolve the concerns over the Juvenile
Temporary Detention Center; and
WHEREAS, the Federal Court approved an Agreed Supplemental Order between the litigants; and
WHEREAS, it is essential that the Board review and ascertain the fiscal impact of implementation of the
May 2006 Agreed Supplemental Order on the FY07 budget; and
WHEREAS, it is also essential that the Board review the 2002 Memorandum of Agreement, the Juvenile
Detention Alternative Initiative (JDAl) Self-Assessment Report, the Implementation Plan, legal fees, and
the progress made towards implementing the requirements as set forth in the May 2006 Agreed
Supplemental Order, the 2002 Memorandum of Agreement and the recommendations as set forth in the
JDAI Self-Assessment Report, the Annie E. Casey Foundation Report and the John Howard Association
Report.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that this Board conduct a public hearing in which the above
mentioned documents and issues are reviewed and addressed.

6

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the communication be referred
to the Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center Subcommittee (Comm. No. 2793 19) and the
Committee on Finance (Comm. No. 279320). The motion carried unanimously.

* * ** *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a governmental corporation which serves and which, by law, must be
responsive to nearly 5,500,000 citizens the governing of which is to be overseen and managed by elected
public officials; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a governmental corporation which provides governmental services to
its constituents with over 25,000 employees who, by law, are to be overseen and managed by elected
public officials; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a governmental corporation which annually expends over $3 billion
in public funds which, by law, such expenditures are to be overseen and managed by elected public
officials; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, by law, is governed by an Executive Department overseen and
managed by the elected President of the Cook County Board; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, by law, is governed by an Legislative Department overseen and
managed by 17 elected County Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, on or about March 14, 2006 Hon. John H. Stroger, Jr., President of the Cook County Board
of Commissioners and Cook County Commissioner for the 4th District was apparently stricken by a
severe and disabling medical condition; and
WHEREAS, from March 14, 2006 to the present date, President and 4th District Commissioner Stroger
has apparently been unable to discharge the powers and duties of his executive office at his official
offices in Chicago, Illinois including, but not limited to, presiding over and attending meetings of the
Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, from March 14, 2006 to the present date, President and 4th District Commissioner Stroger
has apparently been unable to discharge the powers and duties of his legislative office at his official
offices in Chicago, Illinois including, but not limited to, attending meetings of the Board of
Commissioners and its committees; and
WHEREAS, while the executive duties of a governmental official can be perfonned, at his direction, by
appointed public employees, this Board is unaware of specific evidence that President Stroger is, in fact,
personally directing the performance of Cook County government; and
WHEREAS, most legislative duties of a governmental official can only be performed, personally, by the
legislative officer and this Board is unaware of specific evidence that 4th District Commissioner Stroger
is and has been performing his legislative duties; and

7

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

WHEREAS, the members of this Board owe the 5,500,000 citizens of Cook County the fiduciary duty to
ensure that Cook County government perfonns its functions at the direction of its duly elected or
appointed public officials, this Board is presently unsure that this Board has fulfilled and is fulfilling that
duty to their constituents; and
WHEREAS, the members of this Board owe the over 300,000 citizens of 4th Cook County District the
fiduciary duty to ensure that their Cook County Commissioner is capable of and is perfonning his
functions, this Board is presently unsure that this Board has fulfilled and is fulfilling that duty to the 4th
Cook County District constituents; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to Illinois law, this Cook County Board of Commissioners has the legal duty to
detennine whether a vacancy in the office of Cook County Board President or Cook County
Commissioner exists and, if so, to fill any vacancy as provided by Illinois law; and
WHEREAS, the 25th Amendment to the United States Constitution provides a process for the temporary
replacement of the President of the United States during such time as the President is temporarily unable
to discharge the powers and duties of his office and likewise, Article V., Section 6(b) of the Illinois
Constitution ( 1970) provides a process for the temporary replacement of the Governor of the State of
Illinois during such time as the Governor is temporarily unable to discharge the powers and duties of his
office, Illinois law does not presently specifically provide for a temporary replacement of a County Board
President or County Commissioner during a temporary period of disability. However, this Board
concludes that the Home Rule powers of Cook County pennit Cook County to enact an ordinance to that
effect.
NOW, THEREFORE, IT IS HEREBY RESOLVED, that:
I.

Within ten (I 0) days after adoption of this Resolution by this Board, this Board's presiding
officer (or acting presiding officer) shall schedule a meeting of the Committee of the Whole of
this Board to commence at a time and date certain no more than twenty days after adoption of this
Resolution by this Board; and

2.

That the agenda of said meeting of the Committee of the Whole of this Board shall include the
taking of sworn testimony and other evidence on the question of whether the President and 4th
District Commissioner of this Board is presently able to discharge the powers and duties of his
executive and/or legislative offices; and

3.

Further, should it be detennined that the President and 4th District Commissioner of this Board is
presently unable to discharge the powers and duties of his executive and/or legislative offices, the
agenda shall include the taking of sworn testimony and other evidence on the question of whether
that disability is temporary or is likely to extend through and including the remainder of his tenns
which conclude on December 4, 2006; and

4.

Further, that this Board 's presiding officer (or acting presiding officer) shall cause subpoenas to
issue compelling testimony at such meeting by any and all Cook County employees in a position
to have personal knowledge on the question of whether the President and 4th District
Commissioner of this Board is presently able to discharge the powers and duties of his executive
and/or legislative offices including, but not limited to, the President's Chief of Staff James
Wigham; and

8

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

5.

Further, that this Board's presiding officer (or acting presiding officer) shall cause notice to issue
and to be delivered to the President and 4th District Commissioner at all of his official offices, at
all known home addresses and at all temporary addresses notifying him of such meeting, the
matters on the agenda and inviting him to attend and present any evidence relevant to any
pertinent question; and

6.

Further, should the evidence adduced at such meeting suggest that the President and 4th District
Commissioner is presently able to discharge the powers and duties of his offices, this Board 's
duties will have been fulfilled and no further action would be warranted; and

7.

Further, should the evidence adduced at such meeting suggest that the President and 4th District
Commissioner has a present temporary disability which is likely to cease prior to December 4,
2006, this Board 's presiding officer (or acting presiding officer) shall request that the State's
Attorney of Cook County draft an ordinance for this Board's consideration modeled after the 25th
Amendment to the United States Constitution and Article V., Section 6(b) of the Illinois
Constitution providing for a process for the temporary replacement of a Cook County Board
President or Cook County Commissioner during such time as that officer is temporarily unable to
discharge the powers and duties of his office; and

8.

Finally, should the evidence adduced at such meeting suggest that the President and 4th District
Commissioner is permanently unable to discharge the powers and duties of his offices, said
meeting shall then take up the question of declaring said offices to be vacant and filling them as
provided by lllinois Jaw.

It is hereby requested that this matter be referred to the Finance Committee.

Commissioner Peraica, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. Commissioner Butler called for a Roll Call, the vote of yeas and nays being as
follows:
ROLL CALL ON THE MOTION TO SUSPEND THE RULES

Gonnan, Goslin, Hansen, Peraica, Silvestri - 5.

Nays:

Butler, Claypool, Collins, Daley, Moreno, Murphy, Quigley, Sims, Steele, Suffredin - IO.

Absent:

Maldonado, Stroger - 2.

The motion to suspend the rules FAILED.
Subsequently, Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved to suspend the rules so
that this matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
EARLEAN COLLINS, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

REVIEW OF ALL GRANTS AND GRANT FUNDED PROGRAMS FOR
JUVENILE DELINQUENCY PREVENTION IN COOK COUNTY
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII Section 6(a)
of the 1970 Illinois Constitution, and as such may exercise any power and perfonn any function
pertaining to its govenunent and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners is committed to insuring the safety and welfare
of minors in accordance with Federal, State and local ordinances on juvenile delinquency prevention; and
WHEREAS, it is essential that the Cook County Board of Commissioners review all grants and grant
funded programs, including but not limited to, programs for juvenile offenders, crime prevention, social
services and supportive services, involving juvenile delinquency prevention; and
WHEREAS, it is also essential that the Cook County Board of Commissioners review all agencies
awarded grants for juvenile delinquency prevention programs, accountability measures and perfonnance
data.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners conduct a
review of all grants and. grant funded programs for juvenile delinquency prevention and intervention to
ascertain the fi scal and service impact in Cook County.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Daley, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Family Court and Juvenile Detention Center Subcommittee (Comm. No. 279322) and the
Committee on Finance (Comm. No. 279323). The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY
EMERGENCY REQUEST

Transmitting a Communication, dated June 1, 2006 from
BRUCE WASHINGTON, Director, Office of Capital Planning and Policy
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for emergency authorization to repair critical systems
at the Provident Hospital of Cook County affected by a fire which destroyed the electrical panel of the
hospital chiller.
This emergency work is necessary to prevent a breach of the cooling systems during the summer months.
It includes the repair of both chillers at the hospital, replacement of the air handler chiller coils and burner
management system upgrade.
Failure to repair the damaged unit and related coils could jeopardize patient care in the event of extended
inclement weather and place the hospital out of compliance with regulatory agencies.
It is respectfully requested that this honorable body approve this request.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $400,000.00. Bond Issue (28000 Account).
Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved to suspend the rules so that this matter
may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Sims, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the request of the Director of the
Office of Capital Planning and Policy be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

CONTRACTS
Transmitting a Communication from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Cristo Rey Work/Study
Program, Inc., Chicago, Illinois, a not-for-profit corporation, to provide four (4) work/study students
equaling approximately one full-time position for the 2006-2007 school year.

17

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

Reason:

Cristo Rey Work/Study Program, Inc. serves a mostly Latino, low-income community in the
Pilsen/Little Village neighborhood. The students who attend Cristo Rey Jesuit High School
earn the bulk of their tuition through the Work/Study Program serving as interns in various
corporations and organizations. Each student on the team attends five days of work at a
Chicago-area business each month. Class and work schedules are designed so that students
are never required to miss one for the other. The program provides an innovative means of
providing students with crucial hands-on work experience while simultaneously enabling
them to finance a portion of their education. As a result of working in a business
environment, students acquire desirable job experience and marketable skills, develop a
network of business contacts, gain exposure to a wide variety of career opportunities, develop
a strong work ethic, and increase their self esteem. They also provide a significant work
product for the Office of the Clerk of the Circuit Court.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $26,500.00. Contract period: September I, 2006 through August 31 , 2007.
(335-260 Account). Requisition No. 63350039.

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL CONTROL
GRANT AW ARD RENEWALS

Transmitting a Communication, dated May 2, 2006 from
KEVIN GIVENS, Director, Department of Environmental Control
requesting authorization to renew a grant in the amount of $274,500.00 from the United States
Environmental Protection Agency (USEPA). The purpose of this grant is to provide supplemental
funding for the continued operation and maintenance of specialized air pollution monitoring sites in Cook
County pursuant to the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency Air Monitoring Plan for 2006 - 2007.
These sites measure the 2.5 micron-sized particles suspended in the air as part of a new requirement from
the USEPA and are part of a special research project to determine the quantity and composition of these
very small particles in the urban air.
This grant does not require a cash match.
The authorization to apply for this grant was given on February 1, 2006 by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners in the amount of $274,500.00.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $274,500.00. Funding period: March I, 2006 through
March 31, 2007.

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Director of the
Department of Environmental Control be approved and that the Proper Officials be authorized to sign on
behalf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimously.

SPEED LIMIT ZONING ORDINANCE
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 16, 2006 from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Speed Limit Zoning Ordinance
Ashland A venue,
Ridge Road and 17 1st Street
in the Villages of East Hazel Crest and Homewood in County Board District #6
I respectfully submit to your Honorable Body and recommend for adoption, an ordinance revising the
speed limit along Ashland Avenue between Ridge Road and I 7 I st Street, which is under the maintenance
jurisdiction of Cook County. The recommended speed limit was detennined by an engineering and traffic
investigation in accordance with the provisions of Article VI of the Illinois Vehicle Code and as more
fully explained in the following ordinance.
It is respectfully requested that should your Honorable Body concur in these recommendations, the
ordinance be adopted.

06-0-20
ORDINANCE
IT IS HEREBY DECLARED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois, that the basic
statutory vehicular speed limits established by Section I 1-601 of the Illinois Vehicle Code are greater, or
less, than that considered reasonable and proper on the road listed below for which the County has

30

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

maintenance responsibility and which is not under the jurisdiction of the Department of Transportation,
State of Illinois; and

BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that this Board has caused to be made an engineering and traffic
investigation upon the road listed below; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that by virtue of Section 11-604 of the above Code, this Board
determines and declares that reasonable and proper absolute maximum speed limits upon the road
described below shall be as stated herein; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that signs giving notice thereof shall be erected in conformance with
the standards and specifications contained in the Manual on Unjform Traffic Control Devices, the Illinois
Supplement to the National Manual on Uniform Traffic Control Devices and the Standard Specifications
for Traffic Control Items; and
BE IT FURTHER DECLARED, that this Ordinance shall take effect immediately after the erection of
said signs giving notice of the maximum speed limits.
COOK COUNTY HIGHWAY DEPARTMENT
PROPOSED SPEED LIMIT ZONES ON ROADWAYS UNDER
COOK COUNTY MAINTENANCE JURISDICTION

06-R-230
RESOLUTION
APPROPRIATING RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, it is necessary to assure the maximum of service and safety for Cook County Highways and
to determine the quality of such services rendered; and

35

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

WH EREAS, such determinations now require federally mandated structural inspections of bridges on
County Highways: and
WHEREAS, the County does not have the trained manpower or sophisticated equipment to conduct such
inspections.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that such structural inspections be conducted by an outside
consulting engineer in accordance with 605 ILCS 515-701.6, Illinois Highway Code, including
inspections and non-destructive testing of fracture critical and non-redundant steel bridge members and
connections and preparation of written reports; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that such inspections be conducted on four (4) bridges on County
Highways over the Calumet Sag Channel at 104th Avenue, at Ridgeland Avenue, at Crawford Avenue
and at Francisco A venue, as more fully described in an Engineering Services Agreement to be presented
to your Honorable Body at a later date, and shall be designated as (BRIDGE INSPECTIONS STEEL
TRUSS - 2006) Section: 06-6BIST-07-ES-MFT; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Eighty-Five Thousand and
Noll 00 Dollars ($85,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for the completion of
this project; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Clerk is hereby directed to transmit two (2) certified copies of
this Resolution to the District Office of the Illinois Department of Transportation.

June 6, 2006

approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

Traffic Studies
Various locations throughout Cook County
Section: 06-TCIDS-10-ES

06-R-231
RESOLUTION
APPROPRIATING RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, there is an increasing need for intersection improvements including installation and
modernization of traffic signals warranted by traffic movements within the County; and

36

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

WHEREAS, it is becoming increasingly necessary to maximize the service and safety of the Cook
County Highway System; and
WHEREAS, the County does not have the manpower to perform the required traffic counts and prepare
the intersection design studies in a timely manner.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that an outside Consulting Engineer perform the necessary
manual vehicle and pedestrian traffic counts, prepare intersection and link traffic projections, perform
speed analyses, prepare intersection design studies and all-way stop and traffic signal warrant studies and
shall be designated as Section: 06-TCIDS-10-ES-MFT; and

and Noll 00 Dollars ($300,000.00) from the County' s allotment of Motor Fuel Tax Funds for the
completion of this project; and

The purpose of the Community Circles Program is to provide community-based drng
treatment services to delinquent minors who reside in Chicago's North Lawndale Community.
Youth Outreach Services is the lead agency for the program, supervising services provided by
designated sub-contractors, including Westside Association for Community Action, the
Chicago Youth Centers and other local substance abuse and mental health professionals. The
court anticipates serving approximately 350 minors in the next program year. The program is

under the supervision of the court.

provider and child welfare agency, accredited by the Council on Accreditation for Children
and Family Services. Youth Outreach Services has provided substance abuse treatment

DEPARTMENT OF PLANNING AND DEVELOPMENT
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

Transmitting a Communication, dated May 16, 2006 from
PETER C. NICHOLSON, Director, Department of Planning and Development
Re:

159 Halsted Corporation
Resolution Approving Class 8 Special Exception to Abandonment

44

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding 159 Halsted Corporation's application for a Class 8
property tax incentive for your consideration.
159 Halsted Corporation requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month abandonment rule
under the Class 8 Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can complete its
application to the Assessor of Cook County.
159 Halsted Corporation's application for a Class 8, the Resolution of the City of Harvey, Illinois, and a
Department of Planning and Development staff report have been submitted for your infonnation.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 8 that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for a commercial facility;
and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from 159
Halsted Corporation, and the Resolution from the City of Harvey for an abandoned commercial facility
located at 15900 South Halsted Street, Harvey, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Number 29-20-205050-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 8 requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the commercial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive
months upon purchase; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 13.5 months at the time of purchase, and that special circumstances are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners indicate their approval
for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate Classification 8 abatement incentive to the
company for an abandoned commercial facility located at 15900 South Halsted Street, Harvey, Cook
County, Illinois, under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

Commissioner Collins, seconded by Commissioner Quigley, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Business and Economic Development. (Comm. No. 279321 ). The motion
carried unanimously.

Drug Prosecutions Initiative as well as the West Suburban Expansion Program. This program funds the

T he following item was previously approved by poll on May 30, 2006:
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 8, 2006 from
DENNIS MANZKE, Chief of the Administrative Services Bureau, State' s Attorney's Office

54

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

requesting authorization to accept a supplemental grant award from the Illinois Criminal Justice
Infonnation Authority (ICJIA) in the amount of $7,282.00 for the State's Attorney's Victim-Offender
Conferencing Program, a community-based initiative that applies a Balanced and Restorative Justice
approach to juvenile crime and violence. Through this program, the State' s Attorney's Office contracts
with the Neighborhood Restorative Justice Institute, Inc., that coordinates victim-offender conferencing
programs for juvenile offenders in all six Municipal Districts of the Circuit Court of Cook County.
Through this program, trained community volunteers bring the victim and youthful offender face-to-face
in a neutral, safe environment, allowing them to work through their dispute and to create a resolution
suitable to all parties. This project provides a forum for modeling a healthy, positive and production form
of conflict resolution.
The authorization to accept the original grant was given on February 15, 2006 by the Cook County Board
of Commissioners in the amount of $190,507 .00.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Supplemental Grant Award: $7,282.00. Supplemental Funding Period:

and recommended that the said application be granted subject to conditions as stated in the findings.
Vice Chairman Steele, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved the approval of Communication
No. 274481, as amended. The motion carried.

06-0-21
ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE GRANTING A SPECIAL USE LOCATED IN PALOS TOWNSHIP
AS AUTHORIZED BY THE COOK COUNTY ZONING ORDINANCE
WHEREAS, the owner of certain property located in Palos Township described in Section I herein, has
petitioned the Cook County Board of Commissioners for a Special Use permit for a Planned Unit
Development of three single family Jots in the R-4 Single Family Residence District; and
WHEREAS, the said petition was received by the Zoning Board of Appeals of Cook County as Docket
#7999 and a public hearing was held in regard to said request after due notice, all in accordance with the
Cook County Zoning Ordinance and the Statutes of the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the Zoning Board of Appeals entered detailed findings in accordance with the standards set
forth in the Ordinance recommending that the Cook County Board of Commissioners grant said
application for a Special Use permit; and
WHEREAS, it is the determination that said request be granted in accordance with the recommendations
of the Zoning Board of Appeals.

73

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinois:
Section 1:

That a Special Use in the R-4 Single Family Residence District for a Planned Unit
Development of three single family lots as set forth in the Findings and
Recommendations of the Zoning Board of Appeals be granted.
That said property be developed and constructed pursuant to the detailing set forth in the
testimony and contained in the exhibits and Findings of the Cook County Zoning Board
of Appeals, hereby incorporated by reference into this Ordinance, as provided by law.
LEGAL DESCRIPTION

That part of the Northeast 1/4 of Section 34, Township 37 North, Range 12, East of the
Third Principal Meridian, lying Southeasterly of the Wabash Railroad right-of-way, in
Cook County, Illinois.
commonly described as approximately 2.3 acres, located on the North side of 131 st St. , approximately
650 ft. East of Southwest Highway in Palos Township.
Section 2:

That the Special Use permit located in Palos Township of the Cook County Zoning
Ordinance be and hereby is authorized for three single family homes in the R-4 Single
Family Residence District.

Section 3:

That this Ordinance under the provisions of Section 13.7.9 of the Cook County Zoning
Ordinance be in full force and effect from and after its passage and approval, except that
if said use is not established within one year as provided in Section 13.8.14 said Special
Use shall be null and void.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

residence; reduce rear yard setback from 5 feet to 3 feet for a detached garage in the R-5
Single Family Residence District. The subject property consists of approximately 0.07 of an
acre, located on the west side of Luna A venue, approximately 4 7 feet south of 49th Street in
Stickney Township. Recommendation : That the applicant be granted a one year extension of
time.
Conditions: None
Objectors: None

Commissioner Goslin, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved to suspend the rules to consider
Communication Nos. 271702 and 271703. The motion carried.

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Real Estate Subcommittee of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
on Wednesday, May 24, 2006 at the hour of 10:00 A..M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, 11 8 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Subcommittee has considered the following item and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendation is as follows:
277578

HIGHWAY DEPARTMENT, by Wally S. Kos, P.E. , Superintendent of Highways,
transmitting a Communication, dated March 9, 2006:
respectfully requesting permission to discuss the following matter with the Board of
Commissioners, or the Real Estate Subcommittee thereof, pursuant to County Ordinance 950-07 regarding acquisition of real estate.
I . West Bartlett Road,
Spitzer Road to Illinois Route 59
in unincorporated Hanover Township in County Board District # 15
Section: 00-B I 003-05-RP
Parcels: 107, 107PE 1, 107TE I, 107TE2, 107TE3, 107TE4 and 107TE5

*Referred to the Real Estate Subcommittee on 04/05/06.
Chairman Steele asked Superintendent Kos to give an overview of Communication No. 277578.
Commissioner Maldonado noted that the County has an ordinance in effect requiring two license-certified
appraisals for sale of properties owned by the County.
Wally S. Kos, Superintendent of Highways, replied that two outside license-certified appraisers were
hired.
Commissioner Gonnan inquired about the cost of said project.
Superintendent Kos replied that the project is a five-year plan totaling 9.5 million dollars.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved the approval of
Communication No. 277578. The motion carried.
Commissioner Gorman moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado.
The motion carried and the meeting was adjourned.

May 31 , 2006
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Sims, Commissioners Butler, Moreno and Peraica (4)

Absent:

Vice Chairman Goslin, Commissioners Collins and Murphy (3)

Also Present:

Stephanie Milito - Planner, Department of Planning and Development; Joseph J.
Annunzio - Village Attorney, Village of Niles; Patricia L. Jones - Village Administrator,
Village of Palos Park; and Allen Wall - Village Attorney, Village of Palos Park

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Tax Delinquency Subcommittee of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to
notice on Wednesday, May 31, 2006, at the hour of 11 :00 A.M. in the Board Room, Room 569, County
Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Subcommittee has considered the following items and, upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
278877

VILLAGE OF NILES (NO CASH BID REQUEST). Transmitting a Communication, dated
May 3, 2006 from Deborah Sims, Chainnan, Tax Delinquency Subcommittee, submitting a
request from Nicholas B. Blase, Mayor, Village of Niles.
This letter is a fonnal request to place a property located in the Village of Niles, Property
Index Number 09-23-103-065-0000 to be obtained by the Village of Niles through the no
cash bid process.
The property that the Village seeks is situated between residential parcels. It was originally
to be an alley but was never deeded to the Village when the subdivision was created. The
Village wishes to own this property to be able to keep the option open to create an ally when
it becomes necessary. Owning the parcel will also assure the Village of its utility easements.
The Village has an in house counsel to obtain a court ordered deed. The contact person for
the Village of Niles is:
Joseph J. Annunzio, Village Attorney

144

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

I 000 Civic Center Drive
Niles, Illinois 60714
Also, the Village is willing and able to submit to the Cook County Office of Economic
Development an annual report on the status of the parcel for the next five years.
There is no Third Party request for the parcel at the present time, nor will the Village
entertain a third party request in the future.

*Referred to the Tax Delinquency Subcommittee, as Amended on May 16, 2006.
Commissioner Peraica inquired as to the proposed use for this parcel.
Joseph J. Annunzio, Village Attorney, Village of Niles, replied that, because there are sewer and water
piping under this parcel, construction cannot take place on it; it will be utilized as an alley.

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Peraica, moved the approval of Communication
No. 278877, as amended. The motion carried.
278878

VILLAGE OF PALOS PARK (NO CASH BID REQUEST).

06-R-232
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE BOBBIE L. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI AND DEBORAH SIMS
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, The Voting Rights Act of I 965 (42 U.S.C. 1973 to I 973aa-6) has proven to be one of the
most successful and effective civil rights laws in American history; and
WHEREAS, as the Supreme Court has said, the equal right to vote 1s fundamental because it is
"preservative of all rights;" and
WHEREAS, discrimination on the basis of race persists in our nation and equal opportunity in voting
still does not exist in many jurisdictions; and
WHEREAS, in 2007, three crucial sections of the Voting Rights Act will expire unless Congress votes to
renew them; and
WHEREAS, Cook County, with its ethnic and racial diversity, commitment to equal rights and quest to
ensure fundamental fairness in the voting process, believes in the need to uphold the decree of equal
justice for all through either extending or making permanent all sections of the Voting Rights Act.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, BY THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF
COMMISSIONERS, that in relation to the Voting Rights Act, the County of Cook urges Congress to:
I.

Reenact the Section 5 pre-clearance requirements consistent with the time period adopted
with the I 982 extension. These provisions directly impact nine states with a documented
history of discriminatory voting practices and local jurisdictions in seven other states by
requiring them to submit planned changes in their election laws or procedures to the U.S.
Department of Justice of the District Court in Washington, D.C. for pre-approval; and

2.

Renew Section 203 and 4(f)4 so that new citizens and other Americans who are limited in
their ability to speak English can continue to receive assistance when voting. These
provisions currently impact over 466 local jurisdictions across 31 states; and

3.

Renew Sections 6 to 9, which authorize the attorney general to appoint election monitors
and poll watchers. The need for such monitors and poll watchers is paramount to the

147

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

conduct of a free and meaningful democracy. These monitors attend and observe voting
and vote-counting procedures during elections. They watch, listen, and take careful notes
of everything that happens inside the polling place during an election, and are also trained
not to interfere with the election in any way. They prepare reports that may be filed in
court, and they can serve as witnesses in court if the need arises; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that suitable copies of this Resolution be delivered to the President of
the United States, the President of the United States Senate, the Majority Leader of the Senate, the
Minority Leader of the Senate, the Speaker of the House of Representatives, the Minority Leader of the
House of Representatives and all members of Congress representing Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this Resolution shall take effect on the date of its passage and
approval.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Steele, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

06-R-233
RESOLUTION

Transmitting a Communication, dated April 28, 2006 from
DOROTHY BROWN, Clerk of the Circuit Court
On behalf of the Cook County Integrated Criminal Justice Information Systems (CCICJJS) Committee, I
am respectfully requesting that the due date for the CCICJIS Detailed Plan of Action be revised from July
13, 2006 to the new date of December 31, 2006.
The Cook County Board of Commissioners approved a resolution 04-R-257 at the Board Meeting of July
13, 2004 that: I) augmented the membership of the Cook County Integrated Criminal Justice Infonnation
Systems (CCICJIS) Committee and 2) charged the CCICJIS Committee with the development of a
detailed plan of action to support the Cook County Criminal Justice Strategic Plan. The current target
completion date for this detailed plan of action is July 13, 2006. I am happy to report that, although there
have been various delays, we are making good progress towards the development of this detailed plan of
action. However, because of these delays, the subcommittee chairpersons, who are playing key roles on
this project, have asked me, as Chair of the CCICJ IS Committee, if the completion date can be extended
to December 31 , 2006.
The concern of this cross-agency group is that the quality of the detailed plan of action should meet or
exceed the high level of quality established with the development of the strategic plan; and that the
additional time will better position us to achieve this goal. l agree with their concern, and additionally

148

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006
recognizing that these individuals also have full time commitments to their respective job duties and
responsibilities, I fully support establishing a new due date.
Further, on behalf of the CCICJIS Committee, I commit that we will deliver a detailed plan of action that
the Cook County Board of Commissioners can be proud of and one that provides us with a roadmap to
achieving the overarching goals of an integrated criminal justice enterprise: complete, accurate, timely
and accessible criminal infonnation to all stakeholders within the justice environment, resulting in
enhanced public safety while protecting the civil liberties of the Cook County citizenry.
WHEREAS, the Cook County Integrated Criminal Justice Resolution, Agenda Item #79, dated April 23,
2002, established the Cook County Integrated Criminal Justice Information Systems (CCICJIS)
Committee; and
WHEREAS, the CCICJIS Committee was comprised of the major criminal justice stakeholders of Cook
County and the State of Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the Committee was charged with the development of a high-level strategic plan for an
integrated criminal justice information enterprise for Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the CCICJIS Strategic Plan was submitted to the Cook County Board of Commissioners
May 1, 2003; and
WHEREAS, the CCICJIS Strategic Plan detailed the eight strategic issues of Governance, Data
Custodianship, Integration, Privacy, Standards, Infrastructure, Biometrics, and Funding, all which have a
direct impact on the development of an integrated criminal justice enterprise for Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the recommended next step in realizing the goals of an integrated criminal justice enterprise
for Cook County is to proceed with the development of a Detailed Plan of Action, which will draw upon
the eight strategic issues and associated recommendations.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners as follows:
I.

COOK COUNTY INTEGRATED CRIMINAL JUSTICE INFORMATION SYSTEMS
COMMITTEE
The Cook County Integrated Criminal Justice Infonnation Systems Committee is hereby recast.

II.

COMPOSITION OF THE COMMITTEE
A.

The Committee shall be comprised of the following elected or appointed officers:
(a) The Clerk of the Circuit Court of Cook County;
(b) The Chief Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County;
(c) The Cook County State's Attorney;
(d) The Cook County Sheriff;
(e) The Cook County Public Defender;
(t) The Chairman of the Judicial Advisory Council;
(g) The Chainnan of the Criminal Justice Coordinating Council;
(h) The Chief of the Bureau of Public Safety and Judicial Coordination;
(i) The Chief Probation Officer of the Cook County Adult Probation Department;
(j) The CIO of the Bureau of information Technology and Automation;
(k) The Executive Director of the Cook County Department of Corrections;

149

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

(I) The Director of the Cook County Emergency Management Agency;
(m) The Chief of Police for the Cook County Sheriffs Office; and
(n) The Chief of the Cook County Forest Preserve District Police.
The following State of Illinois agencies shall each be invited to designate a
representative:
(a) The Illinois Secretary of State;
(b) The Illinois Attorney General;
( c) The Illinois State Police;
( d) The Illinois Criminal Justice Infomrntion Authority;
( e) The Illinois Department of Corrections;
(f) The Administrative Office of Illinois Courts;
(g) The State Appellate Defender; and
(h) The State Appellate Prosecutor.

The following law enforcement and local agencies shall each be invited to designate a
representative:
(a) The Chicago Police Department;
(b) The North Suburban Police Chiefs Association (District 2 and District 3) - 2
representatives;
(c) The West Suburban Police Chiefs Association (District 4);
(d) The Fifth District Police Chiefs Association (District 5);
(e) The South Suburban Police Chiefs Association (District 6); and
(f) The Chicago Crime Commission.
Lastly, to ensure input from the citizens of Cook County, the Cook County Board President shall
appoint, from the general public, a seven (7) member Citizens Advisory Committee to provide the
CCICJIS Committee advice on community issues concerning integration. It is recommended, but
not required, for members of the Citizens Advisory Committee to have knowledge in the area of
information technology and finance.

III.

B.

The Committee shall seek the input, assistance and participation of other governmental
agencies, private and public interest groups as necessary or appropriate.

C.

The Clerk of the Circuit Court of Cook County shall serve as Chair of the Committee and
may establish ad hoc committees or subcommittees as necessary to assist the Committee
in completion of its mission.

DUTIES OF THE COMMITTEE
A.

To develop a Detailed Plan of Action (specific goals, objectives, metrics and timetables)
for implementing an integrated criminal justice enterprise for Cook County that includes,
but is not limited to the following:
Completing the Data Exchange Pints documentation, developed as a part of the
CCICJIS Strategic Plan, to allow for inclusion of all Cook County municipalities and
defining the processes and events that trigger exchange of information between the
municipalities and other justice agencies.
โข

Developing a clear vision of the 'to be' or ' future' Cook County integrated criminal
justice enterprise, with specific tasks and projects outlined to achieve this vision.

150

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

โข

Documenting current criminal justice interagency business processes and developing
recommendations for future business process improvements which will facilitate
achieving the goals of a Cook County integrated criminal justice enterprise.
Creating the minimum requirements necessary for agencies to share information
electronically, support evolving technologies, and ensure appropriate planning and
maintenance of the IT infrastructure of criminal justice agencies.
Addressing the expanding use of biometrics for rapid identification by supporting
technological applications, and applicable biometric standards for criminal justice
use.

โข

Developing a Cook County Information Privacy Policy that highlights the
appropriate uses of collected, accessed and disseminated criminal justice
information.
Identifying federal, state and other sources of funding assistance to finance the
integration and improving of the criminal justice information systems in Cook
County.
Ensuring that the Detailed Plan of Action complies with national and state integrated
criminal justice standards.
Developing applicable security, verification and audit functions to ensure accuracy
and integrity at every point of the process.
Identifying and with requisite approval, completing near-term opportunities/projects
for improved integration between Cook County justice agencies, and with local and
state agencies.

B.

To develop a process to enable Cook County criminal justice agencies to take into formal
consideration as well as use the Guiding Principles of Integrated Justice, as detailed in the
CCICJIS Strategic Plan, when planning new technology initiatives.

C.

To report the Committee's activities, every six (6) months, to the Cook County Board
President and Board of Commissioners. The first report shall be due six (6) months from
the effective date of this Resolution.

D.

To complete the development of the Detailed Plan of Action withia a hvo year f}eriod
from the effeetive date of this ResolHtioa by December 31, 2006.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.

06-R-236
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE J ERRY BUTLER, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, FORREST CLAYPOOL,
EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,

154

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE AND LARRY SUFFREDIN
COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the observance of June 19th as the African American Emancipation Day began in
Galveston, Texas in 1865 when the word reached African Americans after a two and a half year delay,
that slavery in the United States had been abolished by President Abraham Lincoln's Emancipation
Proclamation on January 1, 1863; and
WHEREAS, that Emancipation Day or Freedom Day has come to be known as Juneteenth Day and is the
oldest celebrated commemoration of the ending of slavery in the United States; and
WHEREAS, Juneteenth Day from its early beginnings in Texas, Arkansas, Louisiana and Oklahoma is
now celebrated in cities across America and beyond; and
WHEREAS, Juneteenth Day acknowledges a period in American history that molded and continues to
influence society where respect is paid for the agony and anguish of slavery; and
WHEREAS, Juneteenth Day now commemorates the freedom of African Americans in the United States;
and
WHEREAS, Juneteenth Day has become a day of pride, renewal and reflection for African Americans
and celebrates accomplishments, education, self-improvement and achievements throughout history; and
WHEREAS, Juneteenth Day celebrations strive to cultivate and promote knowledge and an increased
appreciation of African American culture and history; and
WHEREAS, Juneteenth Day is a day for peace, respect and liberty for all, regardless of race, creed or
religion; and
WHEREAS, June 19, 2006 marks the 141 st year celebration of Juneteenth Day in this nation.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf
of the more than fi ve million residents of Cook County, does hereby resolve that June 19, 2006 be
proclaimed as Juneteenth Day in all of Cook County; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be placed in the permanent
records of Cook County.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin , moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
HONORING DR. ALLAN ALSON
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson is retiring as superintendent of Evanston Township High School (ETHS),
District 202, after 16 years of service to the Evanston/Skokie community; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson began his service to ETHS in 1990 as Assistant Superintendent for
Curriculum and Instruction and became Superintendent in 1992 after serving as a teacher in Philadelphia
and as a teacher and administrator in several communities in Massachusetts, including serving as
Assistant Director of the Boston Public Schools/Boston University Desegregation Collaborative; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson's essential goal as an educator and administrator has been to have all
students achieve and succeed; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson' s commitment to social justice and the critical need to publicly address the
issue of gaps in achievement between white and minority students led him to found the Minority Student
Achievement Network in 1999; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson' s leadership of the Minority Student Achievement Network has resulted in
a collaboration among 25 urban-suburban school di stricts throughout the U.S., which are devoted to
discovering, developing and implementing the means to improve the academic achievement of students of
color; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson's initiatives have beneficially impacted the lives of countless numbers of
ETHS students through mentoring programs, encouraging students of color to register for advanced
placement classes, college entrance exam preparation classes, and instituting an across-the-board math
curriculum, which better prepares students for college and beyond; and
WHEREAS, Dr. A llan Alson' s belief that in order to be the successful high school it is, ETHS must not
exist in isolation and Dr. Alson has promoted and forged substantial partnerships with a diverse group of
citizens, parents, students, community organizations and governments including the city of Evanston, its
business and healthcare communities, and Northwestern and National-Louis Universities. An Interagency

156

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

Collaborative to structure services to children and families in need and a School and Community Task
Force on Safety and Civility have been created through Dr. Alson's leadership; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson is nationally known, respected and recognized as a leader in education,
especially on topics related to equity and the academic achievement of students of color. Dr. Alson has
been honored by the State of Illinois and a local African-American organization fo r his work on behalf of
students of color; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson's excellence as an educator and administrator is exemplified by the
following statistics: Over the last seven years, the college attendance rate for ETHS students of color has
risen more than 10 percent to almost 79 percent; ACT and Advanced Placement scores continue to rise;
the number of students taking calculus has more than tripled since the early 1990s; students continue to
win national, regional and state honors in science research, writing, language, math, business and the arts,
and ETHS's excellence in music, theatre, visual arts and athletics continues; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Allan Alson' s contributions to ETHS and the greater community has greatly benefited
Cook County, the state and the nation; and
WHEREAS, Dr. Alson's new position as a Senior Fellow for the Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation will
allow him to remain an integral part of the community and to continue his contributions to education
reform. At the Foundation, Dr. Alson will serve as an advisor to schools, districts and superintendents in
Chicago and other Midwestern cities as the Foundation strives to effectuate meaningful school reform and
other issues important to teaching and learning; and
WHEREAS, upon his retirement from ETHS, District 202, Cook County owes a debt of gratitude to Dr.
Allan Alson for his inspiring and successful public service and leadership.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Dr. Allan Alson on his retirement from ETHS and wishes him happiness, good
health, and success in his impressive future endeavor; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Dr. Allan Alson
as a symbol of this auspicious occasion and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
ATTEST: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN MEMORY OF CHARLES "CHUCK" RICHARD REMEN
WHEREAS, Charles " Chuck" Richard Remen died suddenly at his home in Evanston on May 19, 2006
at the age of 75 ; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen was the beloved husband for nearly 54 years to Janet, devoted father to
Susie, Carol, Peggy, Tom and Lee, and proud grandfather to Charlie, Austin, Travis, Claire Alison,
Libby, Ben, Annie, Will, Joe, Kaylie and Clay; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen was a wann, detennined, honest and gentle man, who was an Evanston
resident nearly his entire life. He attended Oakton and Nichols schools and Evanston Township High
School for one year, moving then to a military academy in Tennessee; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen attended the University of Michigan prior to serving in the United States
Navy and upon leaving the service, completed his education at Northwestern University and Illinois
Institute of Technology; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen spent his professional life working as a distributor of heating, ventilating and
air conditioning equipment, then as a manufacturer's representative for unique and innovative products in
the same area; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen was an avid sailor his entire adult life, enjoying racing sailboats with friends
at Belmont Harbor in Chicago, participating on eight different Chicago-Mackinac Island races and
sharing his Jove for the sport with his children; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen, upon retirement, found his true passion as an invaluable and philanthropic
community servant; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen joined the Rotary Club of Evanston Lighthouse in 1993 and served as its
President in 1998-1999. While serving on many of the organization ' s committees, Chuck was, far and
away, the leading fundraiser for his Rotary Club's holiday sale; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen, as a Rotarian, assisted in providing playground equipment in San Miguel,
Mexico and more recently, providing a youth center in tsunami stricken areas of Thailand; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen was also an active member of other service organizations including: the
Evanston Chamber of Commerce, INVEST, YMCA, Project SOAR, and the Youth Job Center. Chuck

158

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

also served on the board of directors of the Southeast Evanston Association and the Evanston Historical
Society; and

WHEREAS, Chuck Remen will be joyfully remembered as an entertainer at the Woman's Club of
Evanston's annual benefit shows and as a mentor of countless numbers of children in the community,
forming relationships that extended over decades; and
WHEREAS, Chuck Remen will be deeply missed and forever treasured by all who knew him and the
people of Cook County owe a debt of gratitude to Chuck Remen for his extensive community service and
outstanding civic involvement.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the fami ly and friends of Chuck
Remen and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Chuck
Remen so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

159

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr. was born at Garfield Park Hospital on June l , 1921 and
celebrated his 85th birthday at a party on June 4, 2006 with his many friends and family; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr. was born to Frank and Isola, Italian immigrants, who instilled the
values of respect and love for faith, family and friends to Lawrence, his sister, Mary and brother, Vincent;
and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr. , grew up near Polk and Pulaski in Chicago, graduated from
Crane Technical High School and attended the accounting program at DePaul University; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr. honorably served in the U.S. Anny from January 1942 through
November 1945 and is a decorated veteran, having received a bronze star and two Purple Hearts for
combat in World War II; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr., upon returning to Chicago after the war, married Patricia
Mulrainey on June 6, 1946; they were married over 44 years at the time of Patricia's death in 1990; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence and Patricia were blessed with eight children, Lawrence, Jr., Genna, Paul,
Susanne, Patricia, John, Peter and Michelle, and Lawrence, Sr., is the proud grandfather to 13
grandchildren; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr., served as an officer for the Chicago Police Department from
1946-1950; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr., spent most of his professional life as the owner and publisher of
the Chicago Fruit and Vegetable Reporter, a daily circulation and as owner of the Chicago Produce
Publication Company from 1958 to 1978; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr., was the founder of Westchester Boys Baseball and served as the
organization 's president in Westchester, Illinois and was active in his community as a member of the
bingo team at Immaculate Heart of Mary for 25 years; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr., currently resides at Three Crown Plaza in Evanston, Illinois; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr. is known among his family and friends as a kind, thoughtful
person who continues to maintain his faith and hi s passion and enthusiasm for life; and
WHEREAS, Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr., delights in the achievements and accomplishments of his
children, their spouses and grandchildren.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Lawrence J. Suffredin, Sr., on the occasion of his 85th birthday; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to Lawrence J.
Suffredin, Sr., as a symbol of this auspicious occasion.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President

AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN MEMORY OF JOHN "JACK" LAVIN
WHEREAS, John "Jack" Lavin died on May 27, 2006 at the age of75; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin was the beloved husband of 55 years to Patricia; loving father of Debra,
Colleen, John, Kevin, Mark and Nancy; and devoted grandfather of 17; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin succeeded in three careers during his lifetime; he was a celebrated and honored
Chicago investigative journalist, a public relations executive and later in life, a basketball coach who
helped many realize their dream of playing college basketball; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin learned his street smarts in a family of police detectives and growing up in the
Logan Square neighborhood, attending Our Lady of Grace School, and graduating from DePaul
Academy; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin began his career in journalism at the Chicago Tribune in 1948 as an editorial
assistant. He later worked at City News Bureau of Chicago. During the Korean War, Jack was drafted
into the U.S. Army and was stationed in Alaska, where he worked on Army publications; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin, after the war, became a top news reporter for Chicago papers and in 1957
shared a Pulitzer for helping to uncover corrupt misuse of state funds; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin will long be remembered as the " ultimate in Chicago reporting," often using
clever means to get interviews with famous people such as President John F. Kennedy and the Reverend

161

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

Martin Luther King, Jr. , and bringing the public closer to stories by reporting on many of the most
noteworthy events and famous crimes in Chicago's history; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin, in 1972, left the news business and opened a respected public relations finn ,
The Water Tower Group, where he represented financial institutions, real estate companies, businesses,
politicians and DePaul University, helping to bring the Men's basketball program to national prominence;
and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin represented the hardworking men and women of the Hotel Restaurant Workers
Union for many years working to increase living wages and benefits for all; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin, upon retiring in 2000, pursued his Jove for basketball and worked as director of
player development for Joy of the Game-Rising Stars, Deerfield's Amateur Athletic Union basketball
club and helped many players get scholarships and catch the eye of coaches; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin, in 2005 , the International Press Club of Chicago inducted him into the Chicago
Journalism HalJ of Fame; and
WHEREAS, Jack Lavin will be deeply missed and forever treasured by all who knew him and the people
of Cook County owe a debt of gratitude to Jack Lavin for his many contributions to the community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and friends of Jack Lavin
and joins them in sorrow at this time of Joss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Jack
Lavin so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
AITEST: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Suffredin, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006

MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, hunger and poverty is an issue of grave concern in the United States; and
WHEREAS, according to a study done by America's Second Harvest in 200 I, over 300,000 people in
Cook County relied on food provided by the Greater Chicago Food Depository; and
WHEREAS, in Cook County, the Greater Chicago Food Depository provides food to more than 91 ,000
adults and children each week through a network of 600 food pantries, soup kitchens, and shelters; and
WHEREAS, for 27 years the Greater Chicago Food Depository has served hungry men, women, and
children on a daily basis; and
WHEREAS, the Greater Chicago Food Depository's only mission is to provide food to hungry people
while striving to end hunger in our community; and
WHEREAS, the Greater Chicago Food Depository serves as a model of innovation and service for food
banks across the nation; and
WHEREAS, America's Second Harvest has declared June 6th National Hunger Awareness Day; and
WHEREAS, more than 200 America's Second Harvest affiliates, including the Greater Chicago Food
Depository, will host numerous local events this week to raise awareness of this serious issue.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that June 6,
2006 be declared a day to recognize hunger in Cook County and work towards the prevention of hunger
everyday of the year; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable
Body, and a ceremonial copy of same be presented to Kate Maehr, Director of Development of the
Greater Chicago Food Depository to commemorate this occasion.

Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
AITEST: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

HONORING REVEREND HARDIST E. LANE
WHEREAS, Reverend Hardist E. Lane retires on Sunday, June 18, 2006 after 37 years of service as
pastor to the Fisher Memorial A.M.E. Zion Church of Evanston; and
WHEREAS, Reverend Lane and his wife, Janice, have devoted much of their lives to Fisher Memorial
A.M.E. Zion Church of Evanston, serving its members and the community at large; and
WHEREAS, appointed pastor of Fisher Memorial A.M.E. Zion Church in 1969, Reverend Lane has the
distinction among his colleagues as being the longest serving pastor in his community; and
WHEREAS, in addition to his theological training through North Park College and Garrett Evangelical
Theological Seminary of Northwestern University, Reverend Lane has also been certified by Hazelden for
Pastoral Ministry to Chemically Dependent individuals and their families; and
WHEREAS, Reverend Lane is recognized as a caring and giving community leader, humanitarian, and
outspoken advocate for peace and justice; and
WHEREAS, Reverend Lane has worked to build his church and congregation into a community resource
that provides spiritual guidance and that also helps families and individuals overcome life challenges such
as unemployment, homelessness, hunger, chemical dependency, juvenile delinquency, and learning
challenges; and
WHEREAS, growing from his commitment to provide guidance and help to the members of his
congregation, Reverend Lane is an active community leader who gives his time freely in the service of
others through active membership in community organizations, committees, and conferences and by
serving in leadership positions within these groups; and
WHEREAS, Reverend Lane' s work has been recognized and honored by many organizations including
the Garrett Evangelical Theological Black Seminarians Evanston, School District 65, the Evanston Police
Department, the Evanston Township High School PTA, NAACP Evanston North Shore Chapter, and
Reverend Lane has been awarded the Evanston Friends Meeting Peace Award; and

164

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 6, 2006
WHEREAS, Reverend Lane has never turned his back on a person in need and in fact, has devoted his
life to seeking out and assisting those who most need love, kindness, support, and guidance; and

WHEREAS, Reverend Lane is loved and respected by his congregation, colleagues, and all those in the
community that have been blessed by knowing or working with him on the establishment of numerous
community organizations including the First Base/Fresh Start Programs and the Evanston Community
Development Association (ECDA) which provides affordable and accessible homeownership to low and
moderate income Evanston families committed to building community.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby congratulate Reverend Hardist E. Lane on his retirement after 37 years of service to the Fisher
Memorial congregation and the City of Evanston and wishes him happiness and good health in the
coming years; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to Reverend Lane as
a symbol of this auspicious occasion and let it also be spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorable Body.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.

JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
HONORING 2005 BROOKFIELD FIRE DEPARTMENT FIREFIGHTER BRIAN KLOSS
WHEREAS, Firefighter/Paramedic Brian Kloss has been chosen to receive thi s award for his outstanding
and skilled profession; and
WHEREAS, Firefighter/Paramdic Brian Kloss saved the life of an 84 year old female who had nearly
choked to death; and
WHEREAS, Patrick Lenzi, Chief of the Brookfield Fire Department extends his appreciation to Brian for
his quick actions; and
WHEREAS, Brian Kloss assisted a stranger with his skills when he arrived at the scene, so the patient is
alive today; and
WHEREAS, Brian put his job first; and
WHEREAS, this Honorable Body takes great pride in recognizing Firefighter/Paramedic Brian Kloss to
receive this award.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Cook County Board of
Commissioners wish to extend their thanks for his dedication, leadership, and a job well done.
Approved and adopted this 6th day of June 2006.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
